ويقول: والله لا أتغدى فأما إذا زاد على قدر الجواب فقال: والله لا أتغدى اليوم، وهو موضع الخلاف، فعندنا يصير مبتدأ احترازاً عن إلغاء الزيادة. فبينه المصنف
And among them is what some said: that the general is specified by its cause, and according to us it is only specified by its cause if the general is not independent in itself, like his saying: 'yes' or 'indeed', or it comes in the form of a conditional, like the narrator's saying: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forgot [?] the mosque', or it comes as a reply, and he did not add more. Some: and they are Malik and al-Shafi'i, and followed by al-Muzani, al-Qaffal, Abu Bakr al-Daqqaq, and Abu Thawr. [They say:] The general: if it occurs regarding a specific person in a text or a saying of the Companions and it is not an initial statement. [It applies] specifically to that questioner or the person of the incident, even due to it, whether the cause is a question from a questioner such that someone asked in his presence and he (peace be upon him) answered: 'Whoever does such-and-such, upon him is such-and-such' or 'for him is such-and-such', and he did not say: 'for you' or 'upon you', or the occurrence of an incident such that an incident occurred for someone in a time and the text came regarding that incident, it includes the person of the incident and others. According to these scholars, that general is specified such that the ruling is established regarding others only by another text or by analogy upon them. And the scholars among the early and later ones went contrary to it, and they are supported by the consensus of the Companions and the Followers upon applying the texts that came restricted by their causes to their generality. Do you not see that the verse of zihar came down regarding Khawla, the wife of Aws ibn al-Samit, and the verse of li'an regarding Hilal ibn Umayya, and the verse of qadhf regarding the slander of Aisha [?], and the verse of theft regarding the theft of the cloak of Safwan or the theft of the shield, yet they did not specify these generalities in their particular instances. So it is known that the general is not specified due to the cause of revelation, as stated in 'Ghayat al-Tahqiq'. Then the Shaykh wanted to explain what is the truth according to us and to detail the cause, and he explained it in four sections. [The first section:] 'Independent in itself' meaning it does not independently convey meaning without what precedes it from the cause, and this is the first section. Like his saying in answer to one who said: 'Did I have a thousand dirhams against you?' and he said: 'Yes', or said: 'Do I not have a thousand dirhams against you?' and he said: 'Indeed', so his saying 'indeed' and 'yes' is general due to its ambiguity in that it is suitable as an answer to various types of speech, so when the cause is mentioned, it is attached to it; because each of them is a particle that is not independent in itself, it is not beneficial without its attachment to what precedes it from the cause. So if it is not beneficial without attachment to what precedes it from the cause, how can it convey a comprehensive general meaning? Because that is the characteristic of the independent, rather it is restricted to the cause. But if it was an independent statement by itself, such as if he says: 'You have a thousand dirhams due to me', then it is an initial acknowledgment outside of what we are discussing, so no discussion about it. And the difference between 'indeed' and 'yes' is known in the longer works. [Second section:] Like the narrator's saying: his story with the words of Dhu al-Yadayn: 'Has the prayer been shortened or did you forget?' The hadith is narrated in Sahih al-Bukhari [no. 714] and Muslim [no. 129] and this is the second section. So his saying: 'Then he prostrated' is general, suitable in itself for every prostration, but when it fell in the position of a conditional reward due to the indication of the letter fa, it was specified by its cause which is forgetfulness, and that is because when the speech was made a consequence of what preceded, the preceding was the cause of its obligation, so it attaches to it and does not convey a general meaning. [Third section:] Like one invited to lunch and he says: 'By Allah, I will not eat lunch'. As for when he adds beyond the measure of the answer and says: 'By Allah, I will not eat lunch today', this is the point of disagreement. According to us, it becomes an initial statement to avoid wasting the addition. [The author] clarified it.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage addresses a major usul dispute: does a general statement ('amm) become restricted (yukhass) to its specific cause of revelation (sabab al-nuzul)? The author presents the view of a group of scholars led by Malik and al-Shafi'i, who argue that whenever a general statement comes in response to a specific question or incident, it is restricted to that context unless there is another text or analogy extending it. The Hanafi position is that the general remains general and is not restricted by its cause, unless the statement lacks independence. The author supports the Hanafi view with the consensus (ijma) of the Companions and Followers, citing multiple Quranic verses that were revealed for specific causes yet were applied generally (e.g., zihar, li'an, qadhf, theft). The passage then details four categories of statements that are not independent: (1) words like 'yes' or 'indeed' that require prior context, (2) statements that come as a conditional consequence (like the hadith of the forgetful prostration), (3) statements that come as a reply and do not exceed the answer, (4) a disputed case where the respondent adds more than the necessary answer (like adding 'today'). In the first three categories, the general is restricted by its cause by agreement. In the fourth, the Hanafis say it becomes an independent statement, not restricted, because otherwise the addition would be wasted, while al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Zufar consider the context of the situation (dilalat al-hal) and restrict it. The author emphasizes the Hanafi preference for explicit wording over contextual indication.

Key Terms
العام (al-‘amm): A word or statement that denotes all individuals of its category without restriction.
السبب (al-sabab): The cause or occasion for the revelation of a text, such as a question asked or an incident that occurred.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): Restricting the application of a general term to a subset of its individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a general statement become restricted by its cause?
A) Whenever the cause is a question or incident
B) Only if the statement is not independently meaningful, like 'yes' or 'indeed'
C) Only if the statement is independent, like 'you have a thousand dirhams due to me'
D) Never, because the general always remains general regardless of the cause

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a general statement revealed for a specific cause remains general, a principle supported by the consensus of the Companions, unless the statement lacks linguistic independence.

The Four Categories: When a General is Specified by Its Cause
Detailing the four categories of non-independent statements that are specified by their cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify statements that are specified by their cause into four categories and explain the Hanafi reasoning for each, including the point of disagreement with the Shafi'i school on the fourth category.

Core Idea
Only statements that are not independent in conveying meaning — like 'yes', 'indeed', conditional consequents, or minimal replies — are specified by their cause.

In the previous lesson, we established the general rule: the general is not restricted by its cause unless the statement lacks independence. This lesson unpacks that exception into four detailed categories. The author presents three agreed-upon categories and one disputed, providing the Hanafi justification for each.

Guided Path
1
Recall the General Rule
The general is restricted only when the statement is not independent. This lesson details what 'not independent' means in practice.
2
Identify the First Category: Non-Independent Particles
Words like 'n'am (yes)' and 'bala (indeed)' that require prior context to convey meaning. They are particles, not independent statements, so they are restricted to the preceding question or context.
Example: answering 'yes' to 'Did I have a thousand dirhams against you?' restricts the affirmation to that specific amount.
3
Identify the Second Category: Conditional Consequents
Statements that come as a result (jaza') of a condition, indicated by the letter fa. The meaning is tied to the condition, so it does not convey a general rule beyond that context.
Example: the hadith 'then he prostrated' after a question about forgetfulness — the prostration is specified to cases of forgetfulness.
4
Identify the Third Category: Unadorned Replies
When someone gives a direct answer to a question without adding any extra words, the reply is restricted to the scope of the question. The author says 'and he did not add more.'
Example: if asked 'Who is the man?' and you reply 'Zayd', it is specific to that inquiry.
5
Identify the Fourth Category: The Dispute over Exceeding the Answer
When the respondent adds extra information beyond what is necessary (e.g., adding 'today' to a vow), the Hanafis consider the statement independent and thus not restricted. The opposing school (Malik, Shafi'i, Zufar) still restricts it based on context.
This is the point of disagreement: Hanafis prioritize the addition as making the statement independent, while others see the context as still controlling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

فقوله: "بلى" و"نعم" عام لإبهامه من حيث أنه يصلح جواباً لأنواع من الكلام، فعند ذكر السبب يتعلّق به؛ لأن كل واحد منهما حرف غير مستقل بنفسه، لا يفيد بدون تعلقه بما قبله من السبب، فإذا لم يفد بدون التّعلّق بما قبله من السبب فكيف يفيد معنى عاماً شاملاً؛ لأن ذلك شأن المستقل بل ينحصر في السبب، وأما لو كان كلاماً مستقلاً بنفسه بأن يقول: لك على ألف درهم، فهو إقرار مبتدأ خارج عما نحن فيه، فلا كلام فيه، والفرق بين "بلى" و"نعم" يعرف في المطولات. كقول الراوي: وقصته مع قول ذي اليدين: أقصرت الصلوةُ أم نسيت؟ الحديث مروي في صحيح البخاري [رقم: ٧١٤] ومسلم [رقم: ١٢٩] وهذا هو القسم الثاني، فقوله: فسجد" عام صالح في نفسه لكل سجود، ولكن لما وقع موقع الجزاء بدلالة الفاء خص بسببه وهو السهو، وذلك لأن الكلام لما جعل جزاء لما تقدّم كان المتقدم سبب وجوبه، فيتعلّق به، ولا يفيد معنى عام. كالمدعو إلى الغداء ويقول: والله لا أتغدى فأما إذا زاد على قدر الجواب فقال: والله لا أتغدى اليوم، وهو موضع الخلاف، فعندنا يصير مبتدأ احترازاً عن إلغاء الزيادة. فبينه المصنف
And among them is what some said: that the general is specified by its cause, and according to us it is only specified by its cause if the general is not independent in itself, like his saying: 'yes' or 'indeed', or it comes in the form of a conditional, like the narrator's saying: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forgot [?] the mosque', or it comes as a reply, and he did not add more. Some: and they are Malik and al-Shafi'i, and followed by al-Muzani, al-Qaffal, Abu Bakr al-Daqqaq, and Abu Thawr. [They say:] The general: if it occurs regarding a specific person in a text or a saying of the Companions and it is not an initial statement. [It applies] specifically to that questioner or the person of the incident, even due to it, whether the cause is a question from a questioner such that someone asked in his presence and he (peace be upon him) answered: 'Whoever does such-and-such, upon him is such-and-such' or 'for him is such-and-such', and he did not say: 'for you' or 'upon you', or the occurrence of an incident such that an incident occurred for someone in a time and the text came regarding that incident, it includes the person of the incident and others. According to these scholars, that general is specified such that the ruling is established regarding others only by another text or by analogy upon them. And the scholars among the early and later ones went contrary to it, and they are supported by the consensus of the Companions and the Followers upon applying the texts that came restricted by their causes to their generality. Do you not see that the verse of zihar came down regarding Khawla, the wife of Aws ibn al-Samit, and the verse of li'an regarding Hilal ibn Umayya, and the verse of qadhf regarding the slander of Aisha [?], and the verse of theft regarding the theft of the cloak of Safwan or the theft of the shield, yet they did not specify these generalities in their particular instances. So it is known that the general is not specified due to the cause of revelation, as stated in 'Ghayat al-Tahqiq'. Then the Shaykh wanted to explain what is the truth according to us and to detail the cause, and he explained it in four sections. [The first section:] 'Independent in itself' meaning it does not independently convey meaning without what precedes it from the cause, and this is the first section. Like his saying in answer to one who said: 'Did I have a thousand dirhams against you?' and he said: 'Yes', or said: 'Do I not have a thousand dirhams against you?' and he said: 'Indeed', so his saying 'indeed' and 'yes' is general due to its ambiguity in that it is suitable as an answer to various types of speech, so when the cause is mentioned, it is attached to it; because each of them is a particle that is not independent in itself, it is not beneficial without its attachment to what precedes it from the cause. So if it is not beneficial without attachment to what precedes it from the cause, how can it convey a comprehensive general meaning? Because that is the characteristic of the independent, rather it is restricted to the cause. But if it was an independent statement by itself, such as if he says: 'You have a thousand dirhams due to me', then it is an initial acknowledgment outside of what we are discussing, so no discussion about it. And the difference between 'indeed' and 'yes' is known in the longer works. [Second section:] Like the narrator's saying: his story with the words of Dhu al-Yadayn: 'Has the prayer been shortened or did you forget?' The hadith is narrated in Sahih al-Bukhari [no. 714] and Muslim [no. 129] and this is the second section. So his saying: 'Then he prostrated' is general, suitable in itself for every prostration, but when it fell in the position of a conditional reward due to the indication of the letter fa, it was specified by its cause which is forgetfulness, and that is because when the speech was made a consequence of what preceded, the preceding was the cause of its obligation, so it attaches to it and does not convey a general meaning. [Third section:] Like one invited to lunch and he says: 'By Allah, I will not eat lunch'. As for when he adds beyond the measure of the answer and says: 'By Allah, I will not eat lunch today', this is the point of disagreement. According to us, it becomes an initial statement to avoid wasting the addition. [The author] clarified it.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage addresses a major usul dispute: does a general statement ('amm) become restricted (yukhass) to its specific cause of revelation (sabab al-nuzul)? The author presents the view of a group of scholars led by Malik and al-Shafi'i, who argue that whenever a general statement comes in response to a specific question or incident, it is restricted to that context unless there is another text or analogy extending it. The Hanafi position is that the general remains general and is not restricted by its cause, unless the statement lacks independence. The author supports the Hanafi view with the consensus (ijma) of the Companions and Followers, citing multiple Quranic verses that were revealed for specific causes yet were applied generally (e.g., zihar, li'an, qadhf, theft). The passage then details four categories of statements that are not independent: (1) words like 'yes' or 'indeed' that require prior context, (2) statements that come as a conditional consequence (like the hadith of the forgetful prostration), (3) statements that come as a reply and do not exceed the answer, (4) a disputed case where the respondent adds more than the necessary answer (like adding 'today'). In the first three categories, the general is restricted by its cause by agreement. In the fourth, the Hanafis say it becomes an independent statement, not restricted, because otherwise the addition would be wasted, while al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Zufar consider the context of the situation (dilalat al-hal) and restrict it. The author emphasizes the Hanafi preference for explicit wording over contextual indication.

Key Terms
العام (al-‘amm): A word or statement that denotes all individuals of its category without restriction.
السبب (al-sabab): The cause or occasion for the revelation of a text, such as a question asked or an incident that occurred.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): Restricting the application of a general term to a subset of its individuals.
كلام غير مستقل (kalam ghayr mustaqill): A statement that does not independently convey complete meaning without reference to prior context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a general statement is specified by its cause only when it is not linguistically independent, encompassing three agreed-upon categories and one disputed.

The Invalidity of Conjunction in Necessitating Joint Rulings
Refuting the claim that conjunction in wording necessitates conjunction in ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fallacy of inferring legal parity from conjunction in complete sentences and distinguish it from legitimate conjunction in incomplete sentences.

Core Idea
Conjunction by waw in complete sentences does not force shared rulings; each clause stands on its own evidence.

This passage highlights a common but invalid usul argument: the claim that when two commands are linked by 'and', they must share the same ruling. For example, some argued that because prayer is not obligatory on children and the insane, zakat must also not be obligatory on them, since both are conjoined in the verse. The Hanafi school refutes this by showing that the analogy with incomplete sentences is false. Today we will unpack this refutation and learn why the waw of conjunction does not create legal partnership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
What is the argument being made? The opponents say that because 'Establish prayer' and 'Give zakat' are conjoined, they must share the same ruling, so if prayer is not obligatory on children, zakat is also not obligatory on them.
2
Examine the analogy
The opponents analogize to an incomplete sentence like 'Zaynab is divorced and Hind' where Hind must also be divorced. They claim the same logic applies to complete sentences like the verse.
The analogy is between a complete sentence matching another complete sentence, and a single word matching a complete sentence.
3
Pinpoint the flaw
The Hanafi response points out that the two situations are different. In 'Zaynab is divorced and Hind', 'Hind' is a single word that depends on the predicate. In the verse, both parts are complete independent sentences. Hence the analogy is invalid.
Complete sentences are independent; the waw does not force legal parity.
4
Understand the principle
The usul rule is: conjunction by waw in phrasing does not necessitate conjunction in ruling (al-qur'an fi al-nazm la yujib al-qur'an fi al-hukm). Each ruling must be derived from its own evidence.
5
Apply to the practical case
The thamarah (practical result) is that zakat is obligatory on the wealth of a child (collected by the guardian) even though prayer is not obligatory on the child, because the obligation of zakat is established by independent evidence (e.g., hadith).
This shows how methodological errors can lead to incorrect fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها ما قال بعضهم: إن القرآن في النظم يوجب القرآن في الحكم، مثل قول بعضهم في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلاةَ وَآتُوا الزَّكَاةَ﴾ (البقرة: ٤٣) إن القران يوجب أن لا تجب الزكاة على الصبي والمجنون كما لا تجب عليهما الصلاة لاقترانها بالصلاة في هذا القول، فهما جملتان كاملتان عطفت إحداهما على الأخرى بالواو، فيقتضي التسوية بينهما. المشاركة ومقتضى المشاركة هو إن وجبت إحداهما وجبت الأخرى، وإلا لاتحب الأخرى أيضا. واعتبروا بالجملة الناقصة إذا عُطِفت على الكاملة، وهذا فاسد؛ أي قاس هؤلاء القوم الجملة الكاملة المعطوفة على الكاملة مثل قوله: زينب طالق وهند طالق بالجملة الناقصة أي المفرد المعطوف على الجملة الكاملة، مثل قوله: زينب طالق وهند، فكما المفرد المعطوف والجملة الكاملة المعطوف عليها يشتركان في الخبر وهو طالق لا محالة كذلك الأوليان تشتركان في الحكم.
And among them is what some said: that conjunction in phrasing necessitates conjunction in ruling, like the saying of some regarding the verse: 'Establish prayer and give zakat' (al-Baqarah: 43) that the conjunction necessitates that zakat is not obligatory upon the child and the insane just as prayer is not obligatory upon them due to its conjunction with prayer in this saying. So they are two complete sentences, one conjoined to the other with waw, so it necessitates equality between them. Partnership and the requirement of partnership is that if one is obligatory, the other is obligatory, otherwise the other would not be obligatory. And they analogized by the incomplete sentence when conjoined to a complete sentence, and this is invalid. That is, these people analogized the complete sentence conjoined to a complete sentence, like his saying: 'Zaynab is divorced and Hind is divorced', to the incomplete sentence, i.e., a single word conjoined to a complete sentence, like his saying: 'Zaynab is divorced and Hind'. So just as the conjoined single word and the complete sentence it is conjoined to share the predicate, which is 'divorced' necessarily, so too the first two share in the ruling.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage addresses an invalid argument (wajh fasad) in usul: the claim that if two phrases are conjoined by waw, they must share the same legal ruling. The proponents of this argument used the verse 'Establish prayer and give zakat' to argue that since prayer is not obligatory on children and the insane, zakat must also not be obligatory on them, because the conjunction (qur'an) in wording necessitates conjunction in ruling. The author rejects this as invalid. The error is that they analogized complete sentences (like 'Establish prayer' and 'Give zakat') to an incomplete sentence conjoined to a complete one (like 'Zaynab is divorced and Hind'). In the latter case, the conjoined single word (Hind) necessarily shares the predicate (divorced) because it is grammatically dependent. But in the former, both sentences are complete and independent; the waw does not force legal parity. The ruling of each clause must be determined independently. Thus, the obligation of zakat on children is not negated by the conjunction with prayer. The Hanafi position is that each ruling stands on its own evidence.

Key Terms
القرآن (al-qur'an): Conjunction or joining (not the Qur'an), here meaning the act of conjoining two phrases with a conjunction like waw.
النظم (al-nazm): The phrasing or arrangement of words in a sentence.
الجملة الناقصة (al-jumla al-naqisa): An incomplete sentence, such as a single word (mufrad) that depends on a predicate.

Key Takeaway
Conjunction in wording does not necessitate conjunction in ruling; each independent sentence must be evaluated on its own evidence.

Rule of Partnership in Conditional Sentences
Explains why only incomplete sentences share a condition in conjunctive clauses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a conjunctive clause shares the condition of the first clause and apply the rule of iftiqar to determine the legal effect of such statements.

Core Idea
Partnership in the condition is due to the clause's need for completion, not the conjunction itself.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, when multiple clauses are joined by 'and' in a conditional statement, it is crucial to determine whether the second clause shares the condition. A common mistake is to assume that mere conjunction (atf) automatically extends the condition. This lesson clarifies that the true cause is the need (iftiqar) of the second clause for completion, not the conjunction itself. Through careful analysis of linguistic context, we will see how to apply this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional structure and joined clauses
Locate the condition (shart) and the result (jaza') in the first clause, then note any clauses joined by waw al-ʿaṭf.
Example: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free.'
2
Determine if the second clause is complete or incomplete
Check if the second clause can stand alone as a complete sentence with its own predicate. If it lacks something (e.g., a predicate) that the first clause provides, it is deficient.
'And my slave is free' has its own predicate 'free', so it appears complete—but the context shows deficiency in conditional linkage.
3
Assess the speaker's intent from linguistic context (dalalah al-hal)
Infer whether the speaker intended the second clause to be conditional or immediate. The repetition of a shared element (like the predicate) signals immediate effect.
If the predicate is repeated (e.g., '…you are divorced and Zaynab is divorced'), intent is immediate; if omitted, intent is conditional.
4
Apply the principle: need (iftiqar) causes partnership
Partnership in the condition is established only if the second clause is deficient (muftaqir) and requires the first clause for completion. The conjunction alone does not create partnership.
The author states: 'the cause of partnership is the need, not the conjunction itself.'
5
Distinguish cases where the predicate is repeated vs. omitted
When the predicate is omitted, the second clause shares the condition (need is present). When the predicate is explicitly stated, the second clause does not share the condition (no need).
Two examples: 'and my slave is free' (no explicit predicate, deficient → conditional) vs. 'and Zaynab is divorced' (predicate repeated → immediate).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأن الشركة إنما وجبت في الجملة الناقصة لافتقارها إلى ما يتم به. فإذا تم بنفسه الكلام المعطوف لم تجب الشركة إلا فيما يفتقر إليه، ولهذا قُلْنَا في قول الرجل لامرأته: 'إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق، وعبدي حرّ': إن العتق بالشرط؛ لأنه في حق التعليق قاصر. الجملة الناقصة: وهو قوله: 'وهند'. ما يتم به الكلام وهو الخبر، فإن قوله: 'وهند' كان محتاجاً إلى طالق، فلأجل هذا الاحتياج وجبت الشركة بينهما بخلاف الكاملة المعطوفة إليه كالتعليق، فثبت أن موجب الشركة هو الافتقار دون نفس العطف ولهذا أي لأجل أن الشركة تثبته الافتقار. لأنه أي قوله: 'و عبدي حرّ' وإن كان تاما إيقاعا لكنه في حق التعليق قاصر لأنه بدلالة الحال علم أن غرضه من قوله: 'و عبدي حرّ' التعليق لا التنجيز، ولم يذكر له شرطاً على حدة، فصار ناقصاً في حق التعليق، فثبت احتياجه إلى الأولى في حق الشرط، بخلاف ما لو قال: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق وزينب طالق، فإنه لا يعلّق طلاق زينب بدخول الدار؛ إذ لو كان غرضه التعليق لقال: 'وزينب' بدون ذكر الخبر؛ لاتحاد الجملتين في الخبر، فإذا أعاد الخبر علم أن غرضه التنجيز.
Because partnership (shirkah) is only established in the incomplete sentence due to its need for what completes it. When the conjoined speech is complete by itself, partnership is not established except in what it needs. This is why we said regarding a man's statement to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and my slave is free': that the freeing is conditional, because in terms of conditional linkage it is deficient. The incomplete sentence: his statement: 'and Hind'. What completes the speech is the predicate, for his statement 'and Hind' was in need of 'divorced'. Due to this need, partnership was established between them, unlike the complete sentence conjoined to it like the conditional. So it is established that the cause of partnership is the need, not the conjunction itself. And this is because his statement 'and my slave is free', although it is complete in terms of effectuation, is deficient in terms of conditional linkage, because from the context it is known that his intent from his statement 'and my slave is free' is conditional, not immediate. He did not mention a condition separately, so it became deficient in terms of conditional linkage, thus its need for the first (condition) in terms of the condition is established. Unlike if he said: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and Zaynab is divorced,' for then Zaynab's divorce is not conditioned on entering the house; because if his intent were conditional, he would have said 'and Zaynab' without mentioning the predicate, since the two sentences share the same predicate. When he repeated the predicate, it is known that his intent is immediate effectuation.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a legal rule explaining when a condition applies to multiple clauses joined by 'and' (waw al-'atf). The author clarifies that the key factor is whether the second clause is incomplete (needing something from the first) or complete. If the second clause is deficient (like 'and my slave is free' without a stated condition in its own clause), then it shares the condition of the first clause due to its need. But if the second clause is complete (like 'and Zaynab is divorced'), it does not share the condition; the condition only applies to the first clause. The rule is stated: 'the cause of partnership is the need, not the conjunction itself.' This is illustrated with two examples: (1) 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free' – the freeing is conditional on entry because the clause is deficient in conditional linkage. (2) 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and Zaynab is divorced' – Zaynab's divorce is not conditional because the predicate is repeated, showing immediate intent. The reasoning is based on linguistic context (dalalah al-hal) and the principle of need (iftiqar).

Key Terms
شركة (shirkah): Here, partnership in the condition, i.e., the second clause sharing the condition of the first clause due to its need for completion.
افتقار (iftiqār): Need or dependence; the state of a sentence being incomplete and requiring another element to complete its meaning.
عطف (ʿaṭf): Grammatical conjunction, usually with 'waw' (and), linking two elements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rule explained, what determines whether a second clause shares the condition of the first clause in a statement like 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free'?
A) The presence of the conjunction 'and'.
B) The completeness or deficiency of the second clause.
C) The number of clauses.
D) The mention of the predicate in the first clause.

Key Takeaway
Partnership in the condition is determined by the second clause's need for completion, not the mere presence of the conjunction.

Command After Prohibition and Repetition: Hanafi Usul Rulings
Explains two related usul principles: command after prohibition and command repetition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a command after prohibition indicates obligation (not permission) and evaluate the argument that a command does not necessitate nor admit repetition.

Core Idea
A command after prohibition is identical to a command before it—both indicate obligation; a command is a single instance, incapable of repetition.

This lesson tackles two foundational principles in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the effect of prohibition on a subsequent command and the inherent nature of commands regarding repetition. The passage refutes a common misconception that commands after prohibition indicate mere permission, and it provides a clear linguistic argument against the idea that commands can imply or admit repetition. By understanding these rules, you will gain precision in deriving rulings from divine texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues addressed
Read the passage and note that it discusses (1) whether a command after prohibition differs from a command before it, and (2) whether a command necessitates or admits repetition.
2
Analyze the command-after-prohibition argument
The author states that a command after prohibition is the same as before—both indicate obligation. Examine the refutation of the opposing view using the example of hunting (Al-Ma'idah:2) and the counter-example of killing polytheists (Al-Tawbah:5).
The permission in the hunting verse is derived from a separate source, not from the command itself.
3
Understand the linguistic argument against repetition
The command form (e.g., 'hit') is derived from a verbal noun (masdar), which is a single instance (fard). Since a single instance cannot be composed of numbers, the command cannot necessitate or admit repetition.
This differs from the Shafi'i view that the masdar with the definite article can indicate generality.
4
Distinguish between necessitating and admitting
Even the Shafi'i view only admits possible repetition (with intention), not necessity. The Hanafi position denies even admission because the command's derivation from a masdar strictly limits it to one occurrence.
The practical effect: a single performance suffices; intention of repetition is ineffective (except in cases like slave annulment).
5
Apply the rule to a new example
Consider the command 'pray' (aqimi al-salah). According to Hanafi usul, it commands one prayer, not repeated obligations unless additional evidence is provided. Contrast with the Shafi'i view that it might be repeated to fulfill the generality.
The divergence in practice: Hanafi considers one prayer sufficient; Shafi'i may require multiple performances if the underlying reason is not met by one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأمر
أمر بعد الحظر وقبله سواء، ولا موجب له في التكرار ولا يحتمله؛ لأن لفظ الأمر
مثل: اضرب
صيغة اختصرت لمعناها من طلب الفعل، لكن لفظ الفعل فرد فلا يحتمل العدد.
من حقيقة ذلك الفعل قلنا في قول الرجل لامرأته: "طلّقي نفسك" إنه يقع على الواحد، ولا تعمل نية
الثنتين فيه؛ لأنه لا تصح نية العدد إلا أن تكون المرأة أمة؛
سواء:
يعني إن الأمر في إفادة الوجوب بعد الحظر وقبله سواء، لا فرق فيه. وهذا ردّ على من قال: إن الأمر بعد الحظر أي المنع للإباحة وقبله للوجوب، كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا حَلَلْتُمْ فَاصْطَادُوا (المائدة: ٢)؛ لأن الصيد كان حلالاً على الإطلاق، ثم حرم بسبب الإحرام، فإذا جاء قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاصْطَادُوالله بعد الحرمة أفاد الإباحة. ونحن نقول: هذه الإباحة لم يفهم من الأمر بل من قوله: ﴿أُحِلَّ لَكُمُ الطَّيِّبَاتُ (المائدة:٤)، وإلا فقد جاء الأمر للوجوب أيضاً بعد الحظر في القرآن، كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا انْسَلَخَ الْأَشْهُرُ الْحُرُمُ فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ حَيْثُ وَجَدْتُمُوهُمْ ﴾ (التوبة: ٥)، فإن القتل في الأشهر الحرم محظور، والقتل الثابت بقوله "فاقتلوا" واجب بعده. ولا موجب له إلخ يعنى إن الأمر باعتبار الوجوب لا يقتضي التكرار كما ذهب إليه قوم، ولا يحتمله أيضاً كما ذهب إليه الشافعي، فإذا قيل: "صَلِّ" كان معناه: افعل فعل الصلاة مرةً لا يقتضي ذلك التكرار ولا يحتمله. طلب الفعل . يعنى إنما لا يقتضي الأمر التكرار ولا يحتمله؛ لأنه مختصر من طلب الفعل بالمصدر، فقولك: "اضرب" مختصر من أطلب منك الضرب، كما "ضرب" مختصر من قوله فعل الضرب في الزمان الماضي"، والمصدر المختصر منه فرد لا يحتمل العدد، فكيف يقتضي التكرار وكيف يحتمله وقال الشافعي له: سلّمنا أنه لا يقتضي التكرار لكنه يحتمله؛ لأنه نختار أن المصدر المختصر منه معرف، فهو وإن كان فرداً لكنه اقترن بأداة العموم والاستغراق، فصار بمعنى كل فرد فيراد إيقاع كل فرد وهذا معنى احتمال الأمر التكرار. والفرق بين الموجب والمحتمل أن الموجب يثبت بغير النية أيضاً، والمحتمل لا يثبت بغير النية أصلاً. ولما كان يتوهم (من قوله: لفظ الأمر صيغة اختصرت لمعناها طلب (الفعل أنه كما لا يحتمل العدد ولا يقتضيه كذلك ليس بفرد أيضا، دفع هذا التوهم بقوله : لكن لفظ الفعل الذي اختصر منه الأمر. فلا يحتمل العدد: لأن بين العدد والفرد منافات؛ إذ الفرد ما لا تركب فيه، والعدد ما يتركب من الأفراد، والتركيب وعدمه متنافيان، ولهذا أي لأجل أن الأمر لا يحتمل العدد يقع على الواحد إلا أن ينوي الثلاث؛ لأن الواحد فرد حقيقي متيقن والثلاث فرد حكمي محتمل. ولا تعمل نية إلخ أي لاتصح نية الثنتين في قوله:
And the command: command after prohibition and before it is the same, and it does not necessitate repetition nor admits it; because the word of command (like 'hit') is a form abbreviated from its meaning of requesting the action, but the word for the action is an individual (singular) and does not admit number. From the reality of that action, we say in the statement of a man to his wife: 'Divorce yourself' that it occurs upon one, and intention of two does not work in it because the intention of number is not valid unless the woman is a slave woman. 'Same': meaning that the command in conveying obligation after prohibition and before it is the same, no difference. This is a refutation of those who say: the command after prohibition (i.e., after prevention) indicates permission, and before it indicates obligation, as in the verse: 'And when you are free, then hunt' (Al-Ma'idah:2); because hunting was absolutely permissible, then forbidden due to ihram, so when the verse 'then hunt' came after prohibition it indicated permission. But we say: this permission was understood not from the command but from His statement: 'Permitted to you are good things' (Al-Ma'idah:4); otherwise, the command has come for obligation even after prohibition in the Quran, as in His statement: 'Then when the sacred months have passed, kill the polytheists wherever you find them' (Al-Tawbah:5); for killing during the sacred months is forbidden, and the killing established by His statement 'kill' is obligatory after that. 'And it does not necessitate' etc. means the command in terms of obligation does not necessitate repetition as some held, nor does it admit it as al-Shafi'i held. So if it is said: 'Pray', its meaning is: do the act of prayer once; it does not necessitate repetition nor admit it. 'Requesting the action' means it does not necessitate repetition nor admit it because it is abbreviated from requesting the action by the masdar. Your saying 'hit' is abbreviated from 'I request hitting from you', just as 'he hit' is abbreviated from 'the action of hitting in the past time'. The masdar from which it is abbreviated is an individual (singular) that does not admit number; so how could it necessitate repetition or admit it? And al-Shafi'i said (according to one narration): we concede that it does not necessitate repetition but it admits it; because we choose that the masdar from which it is abbreviated is definite, so even though it is an individual, it is connected with the tool of generality and comprehensiveness, so it becomes meaning every individual, and so the occurrence of every individual is intended, and this is the meaning of the command admitting repetition. And the difference between that which necessitates and that which admits is that what necessitates is established also without intention, while what admits is not established without intention at all. And since it might be misunderstood from his statement 'the word of command is a form abbreviated from its meaning of requesting the action' that just as it does not admit number nor necessitate it, similarly it is not an individual (singular); he dispelled this misunderstanding by his statement: but the word of action from which the command is abbreviated does not admit number: because between number and an individual there is opposition; for the individual is that which has no composition, and number is that which is composed of individuals; composition and its absence are mutually exclusive. For this reason, i.e., because the command does not admit number, it occurs upon one unless one intends three; because the one is a real individual, certain, and three is a legal individual, possible. And intention does not work, etc., meaning the intention of two is not valid in his statement.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage addresses two related issues: the effect of a command after prohibition and whether a command implies repetition. The author begins by asserting that a command is the same whether it occurs after a prohibition or before it; in both cases it indicates obligation. This refutes the view of some that a command after prohibition indicates only permission. The example of hunting (Al-Ma'idah:2) is explained: the apparent permission after prohibition is actually derived from a separate verse (Al-Ma'idah:4), not from the command itself. A contrary Quranic example (Al-Tawbah:5) shows a command after prohibition that imposes obligation. Second, the author argues that a command does not necessitate repetition nor does it admit repetition, countering the Shafi'i view that the command can admit repetition via the definite article (alif lam) indicating generality. The reasoning is linguistic: the command form is derived from a verbal noun (masdar), which is a single instance and incapable of number. The Hanafi distinction between 'necessitating' repetition (which would be established without intention) and 'admitting' repetition (which requires intention) is clarified. The text concludes with a point regarding divorce: the command 'Divorce yourself' effects a single divorce, and intention of two is invalid unless the wife is a slave (where three may be intended by a customary legal individual).

Key Terms
أمر بعد الحظر (amr ba'd al-hazr): A command issued after a previous prohibition of the same action
التكرار (al-takrar): Repetition of the commanded action more than once
المصدر (al-masdar): The verbal noun from which the command form is derived; it is a single instance

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, why does the command not admit repetition?
A) Because the command form is derived from a masdar, which is a single instance
B) Because the definite article in the masdar prevents it
C) Because repetition would require an explicit textual indication
D) Because commands are always for a single action by default

Key Takeaway
A command after prohibition is the same as before—both indicate obligation; a command is a single instance derived from a masdar and thus does not necessitate nor admit repetition.

Transfer of Causation in Deficient Prayer Time
Explains the rule of causation transfer in deficient prayer time and Zufar's differing view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for the transfer of causation (sababiyya) in deficient prayer time and explain the difference between the Hanafi and Zufar positions.

Core Idea
Causation transfers to the last part of time that can accommodate the takbir; Zufar requires four rak'ats.

This lesson explains how the obligation of prayer attaches to time when time is deficient. The Hanafi school rules that the cause (sabab) for the obligation is the time itself, and when only a deficient part remains (the last part that can accommodate the opening takbir), causation transfers to that part. Zufar differed, requiring time for four rak'ats. We will unpack the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept of transfer
The passage explains that causation transfers from part to part as time passes until it reaches the deficient part at the end of the time.
This is based on the principle that the obligation cannot be attached to a part that cannot accommodate the act.
2
Understand the Hanafi measure
According to the Hanafi school, the deficient time is the last part that suffices for the opening takbir (tahrima).
This is a minimal measure, emphasizing that the obligation is attached to any part that can accommodate the start of the prayer.
3
Understand Zufar's measure
Zufar holds that the deficient time must be able to accommodate four rak'ats.
Zufar's view leads to a different application of when the obligation becomes attached.
4
Note the practical consequence
The difference results in different rulings on when a person becomes obligated if they convert or reach puberty at that time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم كذلك ينتقل إلى أن يتضيّق الوقت عند زفر له، وإلى آخر جزء من أجزاء الوقت عندنا، فتعين السببية فيه لما يلي الشروع في الأداء؛ إذ لم يبق بعده ما يحتمل أي في الوقت الناقص أي بعد هذا الجزء انتقال السببية عنده، ومقدار التحريمة عندنا، يتعين السببية لجزء يشرع في الأداء فيه. انتقال السببية إليه: إذ لو انتقلت إلى ما بعده، والواجب لا يسع فيه لأدّى إلى تكليف ما ليس في الوسع. فيعتبر حاله في إلخ : تفريع على قوله: فتعين السببية فيه" يعنى إذا تعين للسببية ذلك الجزء الناقص فيعتبر حال المكلّف عند ذلك الوقت، حتى إن أسلم الكافر، أو بلغ الصبي، أو عقل المجنون، أو سافر المقيم، أو أقام المسافر، أو حاضت المرأة، أو طهرت الحائض يعتبر ذلك الوقت، حتى إن كان الوقت بحيث يسع فيه التحريمة تجب الصلاة على كل واحد من المذكورين وتجب صلاة المقيمين على من أقام في ذلك الوقت وإن كان مسافراً في سائر الأجزاء، وتحب صلاة السفر على من سافر في ذلك الوقت وإن كان مقيماً في الأجزاء المتقدمة عندنا، وعند زفر بحاله يعتبر الوقت بحيث يؤدى فيه أربع ركعات، فإن الوقت باقياً بذلك المقدار تجب الصلاة على هؤلاء وإلا فلا، وقس عليه حال المسافر والمقيم. كما في الفجر: فإن وقت الفجر من الابتداء إلى الانتهاء كامل ليس فيه جزء يوصف بالكراهة، بخلاف العصر فإن وقته بعد احمرار الشمس يصير ناقصاً ومكروهاً. وجب الفرض في جميع أوقات الفجر كاملاً لكمال السبب. فإذا اعترض الفساد بطلوع الشمس بطل الفرض وإن كان ذلك الجزء فاسداً كما في العصر يستأنف في وقت الاحمرار ناقصاً فيتأدّى بصفة النقصان ولايلزم على هذا ما إذا ابتدأ العصر في أول وقته ثم مدّه إلى أن غربت الشمس، فإنه لا يفسد ؛ لأن الشرع جعل له حق شغل كل الوقت بالأداء، فجعل ما يتصل به من الفساد بالبناء عفوا؛ لأن الاحتراز عنه أي عن الفعل الفساد الإقبال على الصلاة متعدّر، وأما إذا خلا الوقت عن الأداء فالوجوب يضاف إلى كل الوقت؛ لزوال الضرورة الداعية عن الكل إلى الجزء، فوجب بصفة الكمال، فلا يتأدّى بصفة النقصان في الأوقات الثلاثة المكروهة بمنزلة سائر الفرائض. بطل الفرض: عندنا خلافاً للشافعي له؛ لأن الصلاة وجبت كاملة لكمال السبب، فلا يتأدّى بصفة النقصان، فعليه أن يستأنف صلاته ودليل الشافعي لله ما رواه الشيخان عن أبي هريرة الله: "من أدرك ركعة من الصبح قبل أن تطلع الشمس فقد أدرك الصبح، ومن أدرك ركعة من العصر قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدرك العصر". [البخاري: ٥٧٩، ومسلم: ١٣٧٤] ونحن نقول : وقع التعارض بين هذا الحديث وبين النهي الوارد عن الصلاة في وقت الطلوع والغروب وفي الاستواء، كما هو مروي في الصحاح فرجعنا إلى القياس، كما هو حكم التعارض، فرجّح القياس هذا الحديث في صلاة العصر، وحديث النهي في صلاة الفجر، وله أجوبة أخرى مذكورة في المطولات. فاسداً: أي ناقصاً؛ لأنه منسوب إلى الشيطان، كما في العصر وقت الاحمرار أي كوقت الاصفرار يؤدى فيه ذلك اليوم بصفة النقصان أي بهذا الشروع الواقع في الوقت الناقص حتى إذا اعترض الفساد بالغروب لم تفسد الصلاة؛ لأنه أدّاها كما وجبت ولا يلزم على إلخ جواب سؤال يرد على قوله، فإن كان ذلك الجزء صحيحاً الخ توجيه السؤال أنكم الآن أثبتم أن ما وجب كاملاً لا يتأدى بصفة النقصان، فعلى هذا لو شرع أحد صلاة العصر في أول الوقت ثم مدّها بالتعديل والتطويل إلى أن غربت الشمس وجب أن يفسد صلاته. فإنه لايفسد إلخ حاصله إنما يلزم الفساد لضرورة ابتنائه على العزيمة، فإن الشارع جعل العزيمة للمكلّف أن يشغل كل الوقت لأداء الصلاة، فجعل هذا القدر من الفساد لأمر العزيمة عفواً. متعذر: فلذا قلنا: لا يفسد صلاته. وأما إذا خلا إلخ بأن فاتت الصلاة عن الوقت. لزوال الضرورة إلخ : يعني إنما يضاف الوجوب إلى جميع الوقت؛ لأن المانع عن جعل كل الوقت سبباً قد زال، وهو كون الوقت ظرفاً مع كونه سبباً، فحينئذ ليس الوقت بظرف بصفة الكمال : لكمال السبب، وهو كل الوقت. بمنزلة سائر الفرائض: يعني لما وجب القضاء=
Then similarly it transfers until the time becomes restricted according to Zufar, and to the last part of the time according to us. So causation is determined for what follows the commencement of performance, since after it there remains nothing that is probable. That is, in the deficient time, after this part, causation transfers to it. So his state is considered regarding Islam, puberty, sanity, insanity, travel, residence, menstruation, and purity at that part, and the quality of that part is considered. If that part is sound, as in Fajr, the obligation is complete. If invalidation intervenes by sunrise—or the lower part—then proving causation for other than the whole and the lower part, which is the part preceding performance, is proof without evidence. Similarly: just as causation transferred from the first part to the second when performance was not commenced. Causation transfers from the second to the third until the time becomes restricted, etc. Its measure is that four rak'ats can be performed in it, so causation does not transfer from it to what follows; because that contradicts the command and the Law. And to the last part, etc., which is the measure that accommodates the tahrima. This is the third division in which obligation is attached to the deficient part. It is the measure in which four rak'ats can be performed according to Zufar, and the measure that accommodates the tahrima according to us. Commencement of performance: meaning in that deficient time—which is the measure of four rak'ats according to him, and the measure of tahrima according to us—causation is determined for a part in which performance is commenced. Transfer of causation to it: because if it transferred to what follows, and the obligatory act does not accommodate it, it would lead to charging one with what is beyond capacity. Then his state is considered, etc.: a branching from his statement, 'So causation is determined for it.' That is, when causation is determined for that deficient part, the state of the obligated person at that time is considered. So if the disbeliever accepts Islam, or the minor attains puberty, or the insane becomes sane, or the resident travels, or the traveler resides, or the woman menstruates, or the menstruating woman becomes pure, that time is considered. So if the time accommodates the tahrima, prayer becomes obligatory upon each of the mentioned persons, and the prayer of residents is obligatory upon one who resides in that time even if he was a traveler in other parts, and the prayer of travel is obligatory upon one who travels in that time even if he was a resident in preceding parts according to us. According to Zufar, he considers the time such that four rak'ats can be performed in it. If the time remains with that measure, prayer becomes obligatory upon these persons, otherwise not. And analogize to the case of traveler and resident. As in Fajr: the time of Fajr from beginning to end is complete, with no part described as disliked, unlike Asr, for its time after the sun turns red becomes deficient and disliked. The obligatory prayer is due completely in all of Fajr time due to the completeness of the cause. If invalidation intervenes by sunrise, the obligatory prayer is invalidated, even if that part is corrupt. As in Asr, one repeats in the time of redness deficiently, and it is performed with the quality of deficiency. But this does not necessitate that if one begins Asr at its beginning and then prolongs it until the sun sets, then it is not invalidated, because the Law granted him the right to occupy all the time with performance, so He made the connected invalidation by building (upon the initial act) excused, because avoiding the act of invalidation when turning to prayer is impossible. But if the time is empty of performance, then obligation is attached to all the time, due to the removal of the necessity that drove from the whole to the part. So it becomes obligatory with complete quality, and it is not performed with deficient quality in the three disliked times, like other obligatory prayers. 'The obligatory prayer is invalidated': according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the prayer became obligatory complete due to the completeness of the cause, so it is not performed with deficient quality. So he must repeat his prayer. Al-Shafi'i's proof is what the two Shaykhs narrated from Abu Hurayra: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' [Bukhari: 579, Muslim: 1374] We say: There is conflict between this hadith and the prohibition reported about prayer at the times of sunrise, sunset, and noon, as narrated in the Sahihs. So we resort to analogy, as is the rule in cases of conflict. Analogy preferred this hadith for Asr prayer, and the hadith of prohibition for Fajr prayer. He has other answers mentioned in the lengthy works. 'Corrupt': meaning deficient, because it is attributed to the devil, as in Asr during the time of redness—like the time of yellowness—it is performed on that day with deficient quality, i.e., with this commencement occurring in the deficient time. So if invalidation intervenes by sunset, the prayer is not invalidated, because he performed as it was obligatory. And it does not necessitate, etc.: a response to a question arising from his statement 'If that part is sound...'. The direction of the question: 'You have now established that what is obligatory completely is not performed with deficient quality. So if one begins Asr prayer at its beginning and then prolongs it by moderation and elongation until the sun sets, then his prayer should be invalidated.' 'Then it is not invalidated...' Summary: Invalidation only follows due to the necessity of its being based on resolve. For the Lawgiver established resolve for the obligated person that he may occupy all the time for prayer, so He made this amount of invalidation for the sake of resolve excused. 'Impossible': so we say his prayer is not invalidated. 'But if the time is empty...' i.e., if the time for prayer passes. 'Due to the removal of the necessity...': meaning obligation is attached to all the time only because the impediment to making all the time a cause has been removed, which is the time being a vessel while being a cause. So then the time is not a vessel. 'With complete quality': due to the completeness of the cause, which is all the time. 'Like other obligatory prayers': meaning when the makeup becomes obligatory...
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi usul work discussing the principle of how obligation (wujub) attaches to time in the context of prayer, specifically dealing with the concept of 'al-amr al-muqayyad' (restricted command). The author explains the transfer of causation (sababiyya) across parts of time when the full time is not utilized for performance. According to the Hanafi school, when time remains deficient (e.g., only enough for takbirat al-ihram at the end), the obligation attaches to that last part. In contrast, Zufar holds that the time must accommodate four rak'ats for the obligation to attach. The passage then discusses the effect of conditions like Islam, puberty, sanity, travel, and menstruation: these are evaluated at the moment the deficient part is determined. For example, if a traveler takes residence during that deficient part, the prayer of a resident becomes obligatory upon him. The author then addresses the case of invalidation by sunrise during Fajr prayer—the Hanafis rule that the prayer is invalid and must be repeated, unlike al-Shafi'i who relies on the hadith 'Whoever catches one rak'ah...' The Hanafi response is that this hadith conflicts with the prohibition of prayer at sunrise and sunset. Using analogy (qiyas), they prefer the prohibition for Fajr (so invalid) and the hadith for Asr (so valid if caught before sunset). The commentary clarifies that starting prayer in a valid time but prolonging into a prohibited time (e.g., Asr prolonged to sunset) does not invalidate because the Lawgiver granted the right to occupy the time, making the connected invalidation excused. But if the entire time passes without performance, the obligation is to make up the prayer with complete quality.

Key Terms
سَبَبِيَّة (sababiyya): The attribution of causation (sabab) to a part of time such that the obligation is attached to it.
الوقت الناقص (al-waqt al-naqis): The deficient part of time at the end of a prayer period that only accommodates a minimal performance (e.g., takbirat al-ihram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the measure of deficient time that determines the attachment of obligation?
A) The time that accommodates one rak'ah.
B) The time that accommodates the opening takbir (tahrima).
C) The time that accommodates four rak'ats.
D) The time that accommodates two rak'ats.

Key Takeaway
Causation for prayer obligation transfers to the deficient part of time that can accommodate the opening takbir.

Applying Obligation at the Deficient Time: Changes in the Person's Status
Applies the principle of causation transfer to changes in the obligated person's status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the obligated person's status (Islam, puberty, travel, etc.) is evaluated at the deficient part of time when causation attaches.

Core Idea
A person's legal capacity (ahlīya) is considered at the deficient part of time when causation attaches.

This lesson focuses on the practical application of the deficient time principle: when a person's status changes (e.g., embracing Islam, attaining puberty, traveling, or taking up residence) at the very end of the prayer time, the Hanafi school looks at that precise moment to determine the obligatory prayer. We'll work through examples from the text.

Guided Path
1
List the statuses mentioned
The passage mentions: Islam, puberty, sanity, travel, residence, menstruation, and purity (from menstruation).
2
Understand the rule
If any of these statuses changes at the deficient part of time, the obligation is determined based on that status.
For example, if a resident travels in that deficient part, the prayer becomes a traveler's prayer.
3
Note Zufar's difference
Zufar requires the deficient time to accommodate four rak'ats for the obligation to attach, which affects whether the status change matters.
If the deficient time is less than four rak'ats, Zufar says no obligation, so status change is irrelevant.
4
Apply the rule to examples
Work through the examples given: disbeliever accepts Islam, minor attains puberty, etc., at the deficient time.
The text states that if the time accommodates the tahrima, prayer becomes obligatory upon each of them.

قوله: فتعين السببية فيه" يعنى إذا تعين للسببية ذلك الجزء الناقص فيعتبر حال المكلّف عند ذلك الوقت، حتى إن أسلم الكافر، أو بلغ الصبي، أو عقل المجنون، أو سافر المقيم، أو أقام المسافر، أو حاضت المرأة، أو طهرت الحائض يعتبر ذلك الوقت، حتى إن كان الوقت بحيث يسع فيه التحريمة تجب الصلاة على كل واحد من المذكورين وتجب صلاة المقيمين على من أقام في ذلك الوقت وإن كان مسافراً في سائر الأجزاء، وتحب صلاة السفر على من سافر في ذلك الوقت وإن كان مقيماً في الأجزاء المتقدمة عندنا، وعند زفر بحاله يعتبر الوقت بحيث يؤدى فيه أربع ركعات، فإن الوقت باقياً بذلك المقدار تجب الصلاة على هؤلاء وإلا فلا، وقس عليه حال المسافر [البخاري: ٥٧٩، ومسلم: ١٣٧٤] ونحن نقول : وقع التعارض بين هذا الحديث وبين النهي الوارد عن الصلاة في وقت الطلوع والغروب وفي الاستواء، كما هو مروي في الصحاح فرجعنا إلى القياس، كما هو حكم التعارض، فرجّح القياس هذا الحديث في صلاة العصر، وحديث النهي في صلاة الفجر، وله أجوبة أخرى مذكورة في المطولات. فاسداً: أي ناقصاً؛ لأنه منسوب إلى الشيطان، كما في العصر وقت الاحمرار أي كوقت الاصفرار يؤدى فيه ذلك اليوم بصفة النقصان أي بهذا الشروع الواقع في الوقت الناقص حتى إذا اعترض الفساد بالغروب لم تفسد الصلاة؛ لأنه أدّاها كما وجبت ولا يلزم على إلخ جواب سؤال يرد على قوله، فإن كان ذلك الجزء صحيحاً الخ توجيه السؤال أنكم الآن أثبتم أن ما وجب كاملاً لا يتأدى بصفة النقصان، فعلى هذا لو شرع أحد صلاة العصر في أول الوقت ثم مدّها بالتعديل والتطويل إلى أن غربت الشمس وجب أن يفسد صلاته. فإنه لايفسد إلخ حاصله إنما يلزم الفساد لضرورة ابتنائه على العزيمة، فإن الشارع جعل العزيمة للمكلّف أن يشغل كل الوقت لأداء الصلاة، فجعل هذا القدر من الفساد لأمر العزيمة عفواً. متعذر: فلذا قلنا: لا يفسد صلاته. وأما إذا خلا إلخ بأن فاتت الصلاة عن الوقت. لزوال الضرورة إلخ : يعني إنما يضاف الوجوب إلى جميع الوقت؛ لأن المانع عن جعل كل الوقت سبباً قد زال، وهو كون الوقت ظرفاً مع كونه سبباً، فحينئذ ليس الوقت بظرف بصفة الكمال : لكمال السبب، وهو كل الوقت. بمنزلة سائر الفرائض: يعني لما وجب القضاء=
Then similarly it transfers until the time becomes restricted according to Zufar, and to the last part of the time according to us. Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi usul work discussing the principle of how obligation (wujub) attaches to time in the context of prayer, specifically dealing with the concept of 'al-amr al-muqayyad' (restricted command). The author explains the transfer of causation (sababiyya) across parts of time when the full time is not utilized for performance. According to the Hanafi school, when time remains deficient (e.g., only enough for takbirat al-ihram at the end), the obligation attaches to that last part. In contrast, Zufar holds that the time must accommodate four rak'ats for the obligation to attach. The passage then discusses the effect of conditions like Islam, puberty, sanity, travel, and menstruation: these are evaluated at the moment the deficient part is determined. For example, if a traveler takes residence during that deficient part, the prayer of a resident becomes obligatory upon him. The author then addresses the case of invalidation by sunrise during Fajr prayer—the Hanafis rule that the prayer is invalid and must be repeated, unlike al-Shafi'i who relies on the hadith 'Whoever catches one rak'ah...' The Hanafi response is that this hadith conflicts with the prohibition of prayer at sunrise and sunset. Using analogy (qiyas), they prefer the prohibition for Fajr (so invalid) and the hadith for Asr (so valid if caught before sunset). The commentary clarifies that starting prayer in a valid time but prolonging into a prohibited time (e.g., Asr prolonged to sunset) does not invalidate because the Lawgiver granted the right to occupy the time, making the connected invalidation excused. But if the entire time passes without performance, the obligation is to make up the prayer with complete quality.

سَبَبِيَّة (sababiyya): The attribution of causation to a part of time such that the obligation is attached to it.
الوقت الناقص (al-waqt al-naqis): The deficient part of time at the end of a prayer period that only accommodates a minimal performance (e.g., takbirat al-ihram).

Resolving Textual Conflict (Ta'arud) through Qiyas: Prayer at Sunrise/Sunset
Explains Hanafi resolution of ta'arud using qiyas in the case of prayer at prohibited times.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi method of resolving textual conflict (ta'arud) using qiyas, as applied to the dispute with al-Shafi'i regarding prayer at sunrise/sunset.

Core Idea
When hadiths conflict, Hanafis resolve by qiyas; here, qiyas prefers the prohibition for Fajr and the catching hadith for Asr.

This lesson delves into the famous dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools about the validity of prayer when part of it falls at sunrise or sunset. The Hanafi school uses qiyas to resolve the apparent conflict between the hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah...' and the prohibition hadiths. The result: Fajr is invalid if sun rises, Asr is valid if one rak'ah caught before sunset.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting proofs
The Shafi'i rely on the hadith from Abu Hurayra about catching a rak'ah. The Hanafi rely on the hadiths prohibiting prayer at sunrise and sunset.
The passage explicitly cites the hadith and notes the conflict (ta'arud).
2
Understand the Hanafi principle for conflicting texts
When texts conflict, Hanafis resort to qiyas (analogy) as a primary method of resolution.
The text says 'faraja'na ila al-qiyas, kama huwa hukm al-ta'arud' (we resorted to analogy, as is the rule in cases of conflict).
3
Apply qiyas to the case
Analogy prefers the prohibition hadith for Fajr because the cause (sabab) for Fajr is complete time, unlike Asr where the time is deficient after redness. For Asr, analogy prefers the catching hadith because of necessity (dharura) for travelers, etc.
The text states 'farajjaha al-qiyas hadha al-hadith fi salat al-'asr, wa hadith al-nahi fi salat al-fajr'.
4
Note the practical difference
The two schools differ on Fajr: Hanafi says invalid, Shafi'i says valid. For Asr, they agree on validity if one rak'ah caught.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the actual ruling for the person praying.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم كذلك ينتقل إلى أن يتضيّق الوقت عند زفر له، وإلى آخر جزء من أجزاء الوقت عندنا، فتعين السببية فيه لما يلي الشروع في الأداء؛ إذ لم يبق بعده ما يحتمل أي في الوقت الناقص أي بعد هذا الجزء انتقال السببية إليه فيعتبر حاله في الإسلام والبلوغ والعقل والجنون والسفر والإقامة والحيض والطهر عند ذلك الجزء، ويعتبر صفة ذلك الجزء، فإن كان ذلك الجزء صحيحاً كما في الفجر وجب كاملاً. فإذا اعترض الفساد بطلوع الشمس سبب أو الجزء الأدنى، فإثبات السببية لغير الكل والجزء الأدنى وهو ما يسبق على الأداء من الأجزاء إثبات بلا دليل. كذلك: أي كما انتقلت السببية من الجزء الأول إلى الثاني عند عدم الشروع في الأداء. ينتقل: قوله: فتعين السببية فيه" يعنى إذا تعين للسببية ذلك الجزء الناقص فيعتبر حال المكلّف عند ذلك الوقت، حتى إن أسلم الكافر، أو بلغ الصبي، أو عقل المجنون، أو سافر المقيم، أو أقام المسافر، أو حاضت المرأة، أو طهرت الحائض يعتبر ذلك الوقت، حتى إن كان الوقت بحيث يسع فيه التحريمة تجب الصلاة على كل واحد من المذكورين وتجب صلاة المقيمين على من أقام في ذلك الوقت وإن كان مسافراً في سائر الأجزاء، وتحب صلاة السفر على من سافر في ذلك الوقت وإن كان مقيماً في الأجزاء المتقدمة عندنا، وعند زفر بحاله يعتبر الوقت بحيث يؤدى فيه أربع ركعات، فإن الوقت باقياً بذلك المقدار تجب الصلاة على هؤلاء وإلا فلا، وقس عليه حال المسافر والمقيم. كما في الفجر: فإن وقت الفجر من الابتداء إلى الانتهاء كامل ليس فيه جزء يوصف بالكراهة، بخلاف العصر فإن وقته بعد احمرار الشمس يصير ناقصاً ومكروهاً. وجب الفرض في جميع أوقات الفجر كاملاً لكمال السبب. فإذا اعترض الفساد بطلوع الشمس بطل الفرض وإن كان ذلك الجزء فاسداً كما في العصر يستأنف في وقت الاحمرار ناقصاً فيتأدّى بصفة النقصان ولايلزم على هذا ما إذا ابتدأ العصر في أول وقته ثم مدّه إلى أن غربت الشمس، فإنه لا يفسد ؛ لأن الشرع جعل له حق شغل كل الوقت بالأداء، فجعل ما يتصل به من الفساد بالبناء عفوا؛ لأن الاحتراز عنه أي عن الفعل الفساد الإقبال على الصلاة متعدّر، وأما إذا خلا الوقت عن الأداء فالوجوب يضاف إلى كل الوقت؛ لزوال الضرورة الداعية عن الكل إلى الجزء، فوجب بصفة الكمال، فلا يتأدّى بصفة النقصان في الأوقات الثلاثة المكروهة بمنزلة سائر الفرائض. بطل الفرض: عندنا خلافاً للشافعي له؛ لأن الصلاة وجبت كاملة لكمال السبب، فلا يتأدّى بصفة النقصان، فعليه أن يستأنف صلاته ودليل الشافعي لله ما رواه الشيخان عن أبي هريرة الله: "من أدرك ركعة من الصبح قبل أن تطلع الشمس فقد أدرك الصبح، ومن أدرك ركعة من العصر قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدرك العصر". [البخاري: ٥٧٩، ومسلم: ١٣٧٤] ونحن نقول : وقع التعارض بين هذا الحديث وبين النهي الوارد عن الصلاة في وقت الطلوع والغروب وفي الاستواء، كما هو مروي في الصحاح فرجعنا إلى القياس، كما هو حكم التعارض، فرجّح القياس هذا الحديث في صلاة العصر، وحديث النهي في صلاة الفجر، وله أجوبة أخرى مذكورة في المطولات. فاسداً: أي ناقصاً؛ لأنه منسوب إلى الشيطان، كما في العصر وقت الاحمرار أي كوقت الاصفرار يؤدى فيه ذلك اليوم بصفة النقصان أي بهذا الشروع الواقع في الوقت الناقص حتى إذا اعترض الفساد بالغروب لم تفسد الصلاة؛ لأنه أدّاها كما وجبت ولا يلزم على إلخ جواب سؤال يرد على قوله، فإن كان ذلك الجزء صحيحاً الخ توجيه السؤال أنكم الآن أثبتم أن ما وجب كاملاً لا يتأدى بصفة النقصان، فعلى هذا لو شرع أحد صلاة العصر في أول الوقت ثم مدّها بالتعديل والتطويل إلى أن غربت الشمس وجب أن يفسد صلاته. فإنه لايفسد إلخ حاصله إنما يلزم الفساد لضرورة ابتنائه على العزيمة، فإن الشارع جعل العزيمة للمكلّف أن يشغل كل الوقت لأداء الصلاة، فجعل هذا القدر من الفساد لأمر العزيمة عفواً. متعذر: فلذا قلنا: لا يفسد صلاته. وأما إذا خلا إلخ بأن فاتت الصلاة عن الوقت. لزوال الضرورة إلخ : يعني إنما يضاف الوجوب إلى جميع الوقت؛ لأن المانع عن جعل كل الوقت سبباً قد زال، وهو كون الوقت ظرفاً مع كونه سبباً، فحينئذ ليس الوقت بظرف بصفة الكمال : لكمال السبب، وهو كل الوقت. بمنزلة سائر الفرائض: يعني لما وجب القضاء=
Then similarly it transfers until the time becomes restricted according to Zufar, and to the last part of the time according to us. So causation is determined for what follows the commencement of performance, since after it there remains nothing that is probable. That is, in the deficient time, after this part, causation transfers to it. So his state is considered regarding Islam, puberty, sanity, insanity, travel, residence, menstruation, and purity at that part, and the quality of that part is considered. If that part is sound, as in Fajr, the obligation is complete. If invalidation intervenes by sunrise—or the lower part—then proving causation for other than the whole and the lower part, which is the part preceding performance, is proof without evidence. Similarly: just as causation transferred from the first part to the second when performance was not commenced. Causation transfers from the second to the third until the time becomes restricted, etc. Its measure is that four rak'ats can be performed in it, so causation does not transfer from it to what follows; because that contradicts the command and the Law. And to the last part, etc., which is the measure that accommodates the tahrima. This is the third division in which obligation is attached to the deficient part. It is the measure in which four rak'ats can be performed according to Zufar, and the measure that accommodates the tahrima according to us. Commencement of performance: meaning in that deficient time—which is the measure of four rak'ats according to him, and the measure of tahrima according to us—causation is determined for a part in which performance is commenced. Transfer of causation to it: because if it transferred to what follows, and the obligatory act does not accommodate it, it would lead to charging one with what is beyond capacity. Then his state is considered, etc.: a branching from his statement, 'So causation is determined for it.' That is, when causation is determined for that deficient part, the state of the obligated person at that time is considered. So if the disbeliever accepts Islam, or the minor attains puberty, or the insane becomes sane, or the resident travels, or the traveler resides, or the woman menstruates, or the menstruating woman becomes pure, that time is considered. So if the time accommodates the tahrima, prayer becomes obligatory upon each of the mentioned persons, and the prayer of residents is obligatory upon one who resides in that time even if he was a traveler in other parts, and the prayer of travel is obligatory upon one who travels in that time even if he was a resident in preceding parts according to us. According to Zufar, he considers the time such that four rak'ats can be performed in it. If the time remains with that measure, prayer becomes obligatory upon these persons, otherwise not. And analogize to the case of traveler and resident. As in Fajr: the time of Fajr from beginning to end is complete, with no part described as disliked, unlike Asr, for its time after the sun turns red becomes deficient and disliked. The obligatory prayer is due completely in all of Fajr time due to the completeness of the cause. If invalidation intervenes by sunrise, the obligatory prayer is invalidated, even if that part is corrupt. As in Asr, one repeats in the time of redness deficiently, and it is performed with the quality of deficiency. But this does not necessitate that if one begins Asr at its beginning and then prolongs it until the sun sets, then it is not invalidated, because the Law granted him the right to occupy all the time with performance, so He made the connected invalidation by building (upon the initial act) excused, because avoiding the act of invalidation when turning to prayer is impossible. But if the time is empty of performance, then obligation is attached to all the time, due to the removal of the necessity that drove from the whole to the part. So it becomes obligatory with complete quality, and it is not performed with deficient quality in the three disliked times, like other obligatory prayers. 'The obligatory prayer is invalidated': according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the prayer became obligatory complete due to the completeness of the cause, so it is not performed with deficient quality. So he must repeat his prayer. Al-Shafi'i's proof is what the two Shaykhs narrated from Abu Hurayra: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' [Bukhari: 579, Muslim: 1374] We say: There is conflict between this hadith and the prohibition reported about prayer at the times of sunrise, sunset, and noon, as narrated in the Sahihs. So we resort to analogy, as is the rule in cases of conflict. Analogy preferred this hadith for Asr prayer, and the hadith of prohibition for Fajr prayer. He has other answers mentioned in the lengthy works. 'Corrupt': meaning deficient, because it is attributed to the devil, as in Asr during the time of redness—like the time of yellowness—it is performed on that day with deficient quality, i.e., with this commencement occurring in the deficient time. So if invalidation intervenes by sunset, the prayer is not invalidated, because he performed as it was obligatory. And it does not necessitate, etc.: a response to a question arising from his statement 'If that part is sound...'. The direction of the question: 'You have now established that what is obligatory completely is not performed with deficient quality. So if one begins Asr prayer at its beginning and then prolongs it by moderation and elongation until the sun sets, then his prayer should be invalidated.' 'Then it is not invalidated...' Summary: Invalidation only follows due to the necessity of its being based on resolve. For the Lawgiver established resolve for the obligated person that he may occupy all the time for prayer, so He made this amount of invalidation for the sake of resolve excused. 'Impossible': so we say his prayer is not invalidated. 'But if the time is empty...' i.e., if the time for prayer passes. 'Due to the removal of the necessity...': meaning obligation is attached to all the time only because the impediment to making all the time a cause has been removed, which is the time being a vessel while being a cause. So then the time is not a vessel. 'With complete quality': due to the completeness of the cause, which is all the time. 'Like other obligatory prayers': meaning when the makeup becomes obligatory...
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi usul work discussing the principle of how obligation (wujub) attaches to time in the context of prayer, specifically dealing with the concept of 'al-amr al-muqayyad' (restricted command). The author explains the transfer of causation (sababiyya) across parts of time when the full time is not utilized for performance. According to the Hanafi school, when time remains deficient (e.g., only enough for takbirat al-ihram at the end), the obligation attaches to that last part. In contrast, Zufar holds that the time must accommodate four rak'ats for the obligation to attach. The passage then discusses the effect of conditions like Islam, puberty, sanity, travel, and menstruation: these are evaluated at the moment the deficient part is determined. For example, if a traveler takes residence during that deficient part, the prayer of a resident becomes obligatory upon him. The author then addresses the case of invalidation by sunrise during Fajr prayer—the Hanafis rule that the prayer is invalid and must be repeated, unlike al-Shafi'i who relies on the hadith 'Whoever catches one rak'ah...' The Hanafi response is that this hadith conflicts with the prohibition of prayer at sunrise and sunset. Using analogy (qiyas), they prefer the prohibition for Fajr (so invalid) and the hadith for Asr (so valid if caught before sunset). The commentary clarifies that starting prayer in a valid time but prolonging into a prohibited time (e.g., Asr prolonged to sunset) does not invalidate because the Lawgiver granted the right to occupy the time, making the connected invalidation excused. But if the entire time passes without performance, the obligation is to make up the prayer with complete quality.

Key Terms
تَعَارُض (ta'arud): Conflict between two textual proofs (hadiths) that appear contradictory, requiring resolution through qiyas or other usul principles.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to extend a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what happens if a person starts Fajr prayer at the very end of its time (so that only the takbirat al-ihram is within the valid time) and then the sun rises during the prayer?
A) The prayer is valid because he caught one rak'ah before sunrise.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) The prayer becomes a makeup (qada) prayer automatically.
D) The prayer is valid but disliked.

Key Takeaway
When hadiths conflict, Hanafis resort to qiyas; for prayer at sunrise/sunset, this results in Fajr being invalid and Asr valid if one rak'ah is caught.
