Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Types of Ada': Mahd, Qasir, and Shabih bi al-Qada'
Classification of performance types with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the three types of ada' according to Hanafi usul, and apply the classification to examples from prayer.

Core Idea
Performance is classified by its resemblance to qada' in commitment and description.

This passage defines three categories of ada' that help us understand how worship is evaluated. A complete performance fulfills the prescribed description exactly; a deficient one lacks a perfection attribute; and performance resembling qada' occurs when commitment to the imam is partially missed. These distinctions are central to Hanafi usul analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
List the three types: ada' mahd (pure), ada' qasir (deficient, within mahd), and shabih bi al-qada' (resembling qada').
Ada' mahd itself splits into kamil (complete) and qasir (deficient).
2
Understand the basis of classification
Note the two axes: (1) whether the act resembles qada' in commitment or time, and (2) whether it is performed with its prescribed description.
Shabih bi al-qada' resembles qada' only in commitment, not in time.
3
Apply to the prayer examples
Analyze the given examples: congregation (kamil), alone (qasir), latecomer (shabih bi al-qada').
The passage uses these to illustrate each type.
4
Examine the rebuttal
Understand why congregation is considered in the ruling of obligatory, making alone prayer deficient.
This rebuttal reinforces the Hanafi position on congregation's legal weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الأداء المحض ما يؤدّيه الإنسان بوصفه على ما شرع مثل أداء الصلاة بجماعة. أي مع وصفه. وأما فعل الفرد فأداء فيه قصور: ألا يرى أن الجهر ساقط عن المنفرد، وفعل اللاحق بعد فراغ الإمام أداء يشبه القضاء، باعتبار أنه التزام الأداء مع الإمام حين تحرّم معه، وقد فاته ذلك حقيقة. ولما فرغ عن سبب وجوب القضاء شرع في أنواع الأداء والقضاء، واعلم أن الأداء أنواع: أداء محض، وهو نوعان كامل وقاصر، وأداء هو شبيه بالقضاء، والمراد بالأداء المحض ما لا يكون فيه شبه بالقضاء بوجه من الوجوه، لا من حيث التزامه ولا من حيث تغير الوقت، والمراد بالشبيه بالقضاء ما فيه شبه بالقضاء من حيث التزامه، والمراد بالكامل ما يؤدّى على الوجه الذي شرع عليه، وبالقاصر خلافه. على ما شرع أي على الوجه الذي شرع عليه مثل أداء الصلاة إلخ مثال للأداء الكامل، فإنه أداء على وجه مشروع عليه، فإن الصلاة إنما شرعت بجماعة؛ لأن جبريل علم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بالجماعة في يومين في الصحاح. فأداء فيه قصور: هذا مثال للأداء القاصر، فإنه أداء على خلاف ما شرع عليه. ألا أن یری الجهر إلخ: تأييد لقصور فعل المنفرد، ودليل على أن هذا أداء قاصر، فإن الجهر صفة كمالية في الصلاة الجهرية، حتى يجب سجدة السهو بتركه فكان سقوط وجوبه عن المنفرد دليل القصور. فإن قيل: ينبغي أن يكون أداء المنفرد كاملاً؛ لأنه هو الواجب بالأمر لا ناقصاً، والأداء بالجماعة يكون أكمل؛ لأن الجماعة سنة لم تجب بالأمر؟ قلت: إن الجماعة في حكم الواجب، فكانت داخلة في الأمر الذي يثبت بمثله الواجبات، فكان تركها نقصاناً. وفعل اللاحق هو الذي أدرك أول الصلاة مع الإمام، ثم فاته الباقي بأن أحدث خلفه فانصرف للوضوء ففاته الباقي. وإن كان هو خلف الإمام حكماً ، فإذا لم يؤدّ كما التزم صار شبيهاً بالقضاء، ولما كان معنى الأداء من حيث الأصل ومعنى القضاء من حيث التبع جعل أداء شبيهاً بالقضاء، ولم يجعل العكس.
Then pure performance is what a person performs with its description as prescribed, such as performing prayer in congregation. i.e. with its description. As for the act of the individual, it is performance with deficiency. Do you not see that the audible recitation is dropped from the one praying alone? And the act of the one who joins later after the Imam finishes is performance resembling qada', considering that he committed to performance with the Imam when he entered with him, but that has actually passed for him. Having finished with the cause of the obligation of qada', he began on the types of performance and qada'. Know that performance is of types: pure performance, which is of two types: complete and deficient; and performance that resembles qada'. The meaning of pure performance is that which has no resemblance to qada' in any way, neither in terms of commitment nor in terms of change of time. The meaning of resembling qada' is that which has resemblance to qada' in terms of its commitment. The meaning of complete is that which is performed in the manner on which it was prescribed; and deficient is the opposite. 'As prescribed' i.e. in the manner on which it was prescribed, such as performing prayer etc. is an example of complete performance, for it is performance in the prescribed manner. Indeed, prayer was prescribed in congregation because Jibril taught the Prophet (peace be upon him) in congregation over two days in the authentic reports. 'Performance with deficiency': this is an example of deficient performance, for it is performance contrary to what was prescribed. The phrase 'Do you not see that audible recitation...' supports the deficiency of the individual's act and is evidence that this is deficient performance. Indeed, audible recitation is a perfection attribute in audible prayers, to the extent that sajdat al-sahw is obligatory by omitting it. So the dropping of its obligation from the individual is evidence of deficiency. If it is said: The individual's performance should be complete because it is what is obligatory by the command, not deficient; and performance in congregation is more complete because congregation is a sunna not obligated by the command? I say: Congregation is in the ruling of obligatory, so it is included in the command by which obligations are established, and leaving it is a deficiency. The act of the joiner is the one who catches the beginning of prayer with the Imam, then the rest escapes him, e.g. he breaks wind behind him and leaves for wudu', so the rest escapes him. He is behind the Imam in ruling. When he did not perform as he committed, it becomes resembling qada'. Since the meaning of performance is from the aspect of origin and the meaning of qada' is from the aspect of subsequence, it is made performance resembling qada', and the reverse is not made.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a classification of types of ada' (performance) by the commentator. It defines three categories: (1) pure performance (ada' mahd), which has no resemblance to qada' in commitment or time change; (2) performance that resembles qada' (shabih bi al-qada'), which resembles qada' in terms of commitment; and (3) within pure performance, there is complete (kamil) and deficient (qasir). The commentator explains that complete performance is performing the act exactly as prescribed, using prayer in congregation as an example because prayer was taught by Jibril with congregation. Deficient performance is performing it differently, such as praying alone, which lacks the perfection attribute of jahr (audible recitation) for the imam. The commentator then rebuts a potential objection: one might think the individual's prayer is complete because it fulfills the obligation, and congregation is only sunna. The response is that congregation is considered in the ruling of obligatory for the people of the town, so leaving it is a deficiency. The third type, performance resembling qada', is exemplified by a latecomer who catches only part of the prayer with the imam: he committed to performing the whole with the imam, but due to a break, he missed part, so his act is performance in origin but resembles qada' because he failed to fulfill his commitment completely. The commentator clarifies this is not termed pure qada' because the origin is still performance. This classification helps understand how legal scholars categorize acts of worship in terms of timing and perfection.

Key Terms
أداء محض (ada' mahd): Pure performance with no resemblance to qada' in commitment or time change.
أداء قاصر (ada' qasir): Performance deficient in description (e.g., praying alone instead of in congregation).
شبيه بالقضاء (shabih bi al-qada'): Performance that resembles qada' due to failure to fulfill commitment fully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Performance types are distinguished by their resemblance to qada' in commitment or description, not by timing.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
6 min
Qada with Rational and Non-Rational Equivalents
Defining two types of qada with examples and textual proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qada bi-mithl ma'qul and qada bi-mithl ghayr ma'qul, and apply the Hanafi rule that extension of the latter is by ihtiyat, not qiyas.

Core Idea
Qada with a non-rational equivalent is proven only by text, but may be extended by precaution due to a shared cause of inability.

In Hanafi usul, not all make-up acts are alike. Some missing obligations can be replaced by something rationally similar (like praying for a missed prayer), while others require a substitute that is not rationally similar, such as feeding the poor for a missed fast. This lesson unpacks the second type, its textual basis, and how Hanafi scholars cautiously extended it to prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of qada
From the passage, note that qada is divided into two types: qada bi-mithl ma'qul (rational equivalent) and qada bi-mithl ghayr ma'qul (non-rational equivalent). Understand the difference: the latter's similarity is not perceived by intellect alone but only by revelation.
The author later adds a third category: qada mahd (pure qada) and qada fi ma'na al-ada.
2
Examine the textual proofs for non-rational equivalents
Review the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:184) establishing fidyah for the elderly who cannot fast, and the hadiths establishing hiring for Hajj. Note how these are taken as direct textual proofs (nass).
The verse is interpreted with an implied negation: those who are not able.
3
Analyse the extension to prayer via ihtiyat
The passage addresses a potential objection: if fidyah for fasting is non-rational, how can it be extended to prayer? The Hanafi answer is that the extension is not by qiyas but by ihtiyat (precaution), based on the general cause of inability (ajz) and the greater importance of prayer.
Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Ziyadat supports this view.
4
Understand the methodological basis: ihtiyat vs. qiyas
Distinguish between strict analogy (qiyas) and precautionary extension (ihtiyat). In Hanafi usul, ihtiyat is a legitimate tool for expanding a ruling when there is a shared cause and a dominant concern for fulfilling obligations.
This distinction is crucial for evaluating the strength of the analogy.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: in the Hanafi school, the heir of a deceased who owed prayers and bequeathed fidyah must pay fidyah for prayers; other schools reject this. This shows the real impact of the usul principle.
The madhhab dispute map in the lesson details this.

Statement of the attribute of the ruling of the command. And for this reason his obligation does not change by the intention of residence in this situation, just as if it became pure qada due to lapse. Then the situation changes, unlike the latecomer; because he is performing the remainder of his prayer. [Types of Qada] Qada is of two types: qada with a rationally understandable equivalent as we mentioned, and with a non-rational equivalent, like the fidyah in the chapter of fasting for the elderly person, and hiring someone for Hajj, both established by text. And for this: meaning because it resembles qada. 'His obligation does not change' etc. This is the result of it being similar to qada. Its clarification: if this follower was a traveler and followed a traveler, then he broke his wudu and went to his city for wudu, or he intended residence in his place, then came after the imam finished and did not speak and began completing the prayer, then he does not complete four but prays two rak'ahs. 'Just as if it became' etc.: meaning he does not pray four in what became qada due to lapse, then the situation changed by intending residence, likewise he does not pray four in the mentioned scenario. But if he followed a resident rather than a traveler, or the imam had not finished, or he spoke and then restarted, or the case is like that of the latecomer, then their obligation becomes four by intention of residence. And to the latecomer he refers by saying: unlike the latecomer: that a traveler follows in time after the imam has prayed one rak'ah. When the imam completed his prayer, the follower intends residence, then he completes four. 'Completing his prayer': meaning he is not a qada in the remaining amount but is performing it in all respects; because time remains and he did not commit to performing this amount with the imam. So when he is performing, his intention has effect, so his obligation changes by intention of residence and becomes four. :Two types. And it is better to say: Qada has types: pure qada, and it is either with a rationally understandable equivalent or with a non-rational equivalent, and qada in the sense of performance. Pure qada means that there is no meaning of performance in it at all, neither in reality nor by ruling. What is meant by qada in the sense of performance is the opposite. By rationally understandable equivalent is meant that its similarity is perceived by the intellect without regard to the Law, and by non-rational equivalent that its similarity is not perceived except by the Law. Qada necessarily requires a new cause by agreement, but the author distinguished pure qada, so what is meant by his saying 'performance' is this section. 'Qada is of two types: pure qada, and it is of two types as we mentioned: qada of prayer with prayer and fasting with fasting. The elderly person: is the one who is unable to fast due to weakness, so he must pay fidyah for each day half a sa' of wheat or his flour or his semolina or raisins, or a sa' of dates or barley. And hiring someone for Hajj: for one who is unable to perform Hajj due to permanent inability, he must order another to perform Hajj on his behalf and give him the money to perform it. Both are established by text. By text: which regarding fidyah is His statement: 'And upon those who are able to fast, a fidyah of feeding a poor person' (al-Baqarah 2:184) with the word 'not' being implied, i.e., they are not able, as in His statement: 'Allah makes clear to you lest you go astray' (al-Nisa 4:176), meaning so that you do not go astray, or the hamzah is for negation. And we do not rationally understand similarity between fasting and fidyah, nor between Hajj and expenditure. But it is possible that the text obligating fidyah is caused by the cause of inability, and prayer is analogous to fasting, indeed it is more important, so we ordered fidyah for prayer as a precaution, hoping for acceptance from Allah as a favor. Then Muhammad said in al-Ziyadat: meaning they are stripped of ability. Otherwise the verse is abrogated according to what was said: at the beginning of Islam, the one able was given a choice between fasting and paying fidyah, then it was abrogated. And regarding hiring for Hajj, the hadith is that a woman from Khath'am said: O Messenger of Allah, the obligation of Allah upon His servants regarding Hajj has reached my father, an old man who cannot sit firmly on the mount, should I perform Hajj on his behalf? He said: Yes. That was during the Farewell Pilgrimage. (Agreed upon) And from Ibn Abbas: A man came to the Prophet and said: My sister vowed to perform Hajj and then died. The Prophet said: 'If she had a debt, would you pay it?' He said: Yes. He said: 'Then pay the debt of Allah, which is more deserving of being paid.' (Agreed upon) [Bukhari, no. 6699] I say: In most narrations it is 'ahajju' with fatha on hamza and damm on ha, meaning I will enter ihram for him and perform the actions of Hajj for him. According to this, there is no indication in the hadith that expenditure stands in place of Hajj, so it is not correct to use this hadith as proof unless the meaning of her saying 'that I perform Hajj' is that I order someone to perform Hajj for him. In some narrations 'uhajju' with damm on hamza and kasr on ha, meaning I order someone to perform Hajj for him, so the use is correct. 'And we do not rationally understand similarity' etc. As for form, it is apparent; as for meaning, because fasting is starving the self, while fidyah is satiating. And not between Hajj and expenditure: as for form it is apparent; as for meaning, because expenditure is a substance while Hajj is actions which are accidents. The gist is that qada of fasting with fidyah and qada of Hajj with expenditure is qada with a non-rational equivalent, since there is no similarity between fasting and fidyah nor between Hajj and expenditure. They are only established by text alone. And prayer is analogous to fasting: in that each is a purely physical act of worship, their obligation and performance have no connection to wealth. Fasting is an act of worship in itself because it is veneration of Allah by itself, unlike fasting which is worship through subduing the self. 'With fidyah for prayer' etc. is an answer to an implied question. The implied question is: since the fidyah for fasting for the elderly person was of unintelligible meaning and was established by text, it is not permissible to analogize fidyah for prayer to it, even though you say that one who dies owing prayers and bequeathed fidyah, the heir must pay fidyah for each prayer in the amount of fidyah for each fast according to the chosen school. The answer: the obligation of fidyah in making up prayer is for precaution, not for analogy. This is because the text obligating fidyah for fasting is possibly specific to it, and possibly caused by a general cause: inability. So just as we were commanded regarding fasting due to inability to pay fidyah, likewise we are commanded regarding prayer due to inability to pay fidyah. Indeed, prayer is more important than fasting, so we ordered fidyah for it as a precaution. If it suffices, then good; otherwise, he will have the reward of charity.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a commentary defining the types of qada (making up missed obligations) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by explaining the previous statement about a traveler following an imam: due to the situation resembling qada, the obligation does not change by intention of residence. He then distinguishes between the latecomer (masbuq) who is performing the remainder of his prayer, so his obligation can change. This leads into the main topic: types of qada. Qada is divided into two: qada with a rationally understandable equivalent (e.g., making up prayer with prayer, fasting with fasting) and qada with a non-rational equivalent that is established only by nass (text), such as fidyah for fasting in place of fasting for the elderly person who cannot fast, and hiring someone for Hajj for the permanently unable. These are called 'ghayr ma'qul' because our intellect does not perceive similarity between fasting and feeding the poor, or between Hajj and spending money. The fidyah for fasting is from Quran 2:184, interpreted as applying to those who cannot fast. The hadith about the woman from Khath'am and Ibn Abbas's narration establish hiring for Hajj. The author then addresses a potential objection: if fidyah for fasting is non-rational, how can we analogize it to prayer? He explains that it is not analogy but precaution (ihtiyat); the text for fasting may have a general cause (inability), and prayer is even more important, so we apply fidyah for prayer similarly as a precaution. The passage concludes with the ruling from Imam Muhammad in al-Ziyadat that fidyah for prayer is valid based on this reasoning. The key usul principle is that qada can be with a non-rational equivalent if the text establishes it, and extension to other cases is based on precaution, not strict analogy.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory act of worship after its prescribed time has passed.
قضاء محض (qada mahd): Pure qada that contains no element of performance (ada) at all, neither in reality nor by ruling.
قضاء بمثل معقول (qada bi-mithl ma'qul): Qada where the substitute is rationally similar to the original act, such as qada of prayer with prayer.
قضاء بمثل غير معقول (qada bi-mithl ghayr ma'qul): Qada where the substitute is not rationally similar to the original, established only by nass (text).
فدية (fidyah): A compensatory payment (usually food) in place of a missed fast due to permanent inability.
إحجاج الغير (ihjaj al-ghayr): Hiring or commissioning someone else to perform Hajj on behalf of a person who is permanently unable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the Hanafi ruling that fidyah is required for missed prayers for a permanently unable person?
A) Qiyas to fidyah for fasting
B) Ihtiyat (precaution) due to the general cause of inability
C) Direct Quranic text mentioning prayer
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qada with a non-rational equivalent (like fidyah) is established by text, but its extension to other cases is permissible through ihtiyat (precaution), not qiyas, based on a shared cause of inability.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
Evil for Itself (Qabih li-Aynihi) in Hanafi Usul
Classification of prohibitions evil by essence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two subtypes of qabih li-aynihi and explain why acts like prayer without wudu are annexed to the inherently evil category.

Core Idea
An act evil by its essence is either recognized by intellect or annexed by law due to lack of capacity.

The Hanafi school classifies prohibitions by the source of their evilness. This lesson unpacks the first major category: evil for itself (qabih li-aynihi), including both inherent evils like kufr and legally annexed acts like prayer without wudu. Understanding this classification is key to grasping why some prohibitions are immutable while others are contingent on legal capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories of prohibition
The text divides prohibitions into evil for itself and evil due to another. Focus on the first.
The second category will be covered in the next lesson.
2
Recognize the first subtype: evil by primary disposition (wad'an)
Acts like kufr and al-`abath are evil by intellect; they cannot be abrogated.
These are recognized as evil before revelation (bi-al-`aql).
3
Recognize the second subtype: annexed by legal incapacity
Acts like salat al-muhdith and bay` al-hurr are not inherently evil but become so because the Law deems them lacking capacity, thus annexed to the first subtype.
The annexation is due to 'adam al-ahliyya or 'adam al-mahalliyya.
4
Apply the ruling of these prohibitions
The ruling is that the act is fundamentally unlegislated (ghayr mashru` aslan); it is invalid and void.
This contrasts with prohibitions that affect only the circumstance.
5
Distinguish from evil due to another
Note that this category is fundamentally different from acts that are permissible in essence but prohibited due to external factors.
The distinction determines whether the act is void or merely sinful.

فصل في النهي وهو في صفة القبح ينقسم انقسام الأمر في صفة الحسن. نوعا القبيح لعينه وحكمهما ] ما قبح لعينه وضعاً كالكفر والعبث وما التحق به بواسطة عدم الأهلية والمحلية شرعاً، كصلاة المحدث وبيع الحرّ والمضامين والملاقيح وحكم النهي فيهما بيان أنه غير مشروع أصلاً. وما قبح لمعنى في غيره وهو نوعان ما جاوره المعنى جمعاً كالبيع وقت النداء، والصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة والوطي في حالة الحيض، فهذا القسم الرابع يعني القسم الرابع ما جاور المنهي عنه الغير الذي قبح لأجله ذلك المنهي عنه جمعاً بأن يجتمعا في بعض الأحيان من غير أن ذلك الغير وصفاً لازماً له أو داخلاً في حقيقته. كالبيع وقت أذان الجمعة أمر مشروع في ذاته، وإنما قبح بالإخلال بالسعي الواجب إلى الجمعة وهو أمر مجاور للبيع قابل للانفكاك عنه، فإن البيع قد جد بغير الإخلال بأن يبيعا في الطريق ذاهبين إلى الجامع، والإخلال بالسعي قد يوجد بدون البيع بأن يمكث في الطريق بغير البيع، وكذا الصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة مشروعة في ذاتها، وإنما قبحت لأجل شغل ملك الغير، وهو أمر ينفك الصلاة بأن يوجد الصلاة في ملك نفسه، ويوجد الشغل بغير الصلاة بأن يسكن فيها عن ذلك.
Chapter on Prohibition. It, in the attribute of evilness, divides as the command divides in the attribute of goodness. The two types of evil for itself and their ruling... That which is evil for itself by primary disposition such as disbelief and vain action, and what is attached to it by way of lack of capacity or legality according to the Law, like the prayer of a person in hadath, the sale of a free person, the sales of 'madamin' and 'malaqih', and the ruling of prohibition in them is that it is not legislated at all. And that which is evil due to a meaning in something else, and it is two types: one is that the meaning accompanies it collectively, like sale at the time of the call (to Friday prayer), and prayer in usurped land, and intercourse during menstruation. This is the fourth division: that which accompanies the prohibited thing, the other thing for which the prohibited is evil, collectively, such that they come together at some times without that other thing being a necessary attribute of it or entering its essence. Like sale at the time of the Friday adhan: it is permissible in itself, but it becomes evil due to abandoning the obligatory going to Friday prayer, which is an accompanying matter separable from the sale, for the sale can occur without abandonment (e.g., they sell on the way going to the mosque), and abandonment can occur without sale (e.g., he delays on the way without selling). Similarly, prayer in usurped land is permissible in itself, but it becomes evil because of occupying another's property, which is separable from prayer: prayer can occur in one's own property, and occupation can occur without prayer (e.g., he dwells there without praying).
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul text defines the division of prohibitions (nahy) into types according to their inherent or acquired evilness. The author states that prohibitions, in terms of being evil (qabih), are divided just as commands are divided in terms of being good (hasan). There are two primary categories: something evil for itself (qabih li-aynihi) and something evil due to something else (qabih li-ghayrihi). 

Within 'evil for itself', there are two subcategories: (1) what is evil by primary disposition (wad'an), like disbelief (kufr) and vain action (al-`abath). Disbelief is recognized by intellect as evil because it is ingratitude to the Benefactor, and thus its prohibition cannot be abrogated. (2) What is attached to the first category by way of lack of capacity or legality according to the Law, such as the prayer of a person without wudu (salat al-muhdith), the sale of a free person, and the sales of 'madamin' (what is in the loins of stallions) and 'malaqih' (what is in the wombs). These acts are not inherently evil by intellect, but the Law has made them impermissible due to lack of capacity (for prayer without wudu) or lack of legality (for sale of a free person or unborn animals). Thus they are annexed to the first category.

Then 'evil due to something else' has two types: (1) that in which the evil-making meaning accompanies the prohibited act collectively (jami'an), like sale during the Friday call to prayer, prayer in usurped land, and intercourse during menstruation. (2) The fourth overall division (since the first two are types of evil for itself) is when the accompanying meaning is separable (mujawir). The author explains that the evil here is not in the act itself but in the concomitant circumstance that can be separated. For example, sale at the time of Friday adhan: sale is permissible in itself, but it becomes evil because it leads to abandoning the obligation of going to Friday prayer. This abandonment can be separated from sale (one can sell while walking to the mosque without abandoning the obligation) and vice versa. Similarly, prayer in usurped land is good in itself but becomes evil because of occupying another's property, which can be separated.

The author concludes that the ruling for the first two types (evil for itself and annexed) is that the act is fundamentally unlegislated (laysa bi mashru` aslan), while for the latter types the act is permissible in principle but prohibited due to an external factor.

Key Terms
قبيح لعينه (qabīḥ li-‘aynihī): Something evil in its own essence, whether by intellect (like kufr) or by Law (like prayer without wudu annexed to it).
وضعاً (waḍ‘an): By primary disposition or original constitution, recognized by intellect before revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul classification, why is the sale of a free person (bay‘ al-ḥurr) considered prohibited?
A) Because selling a human is inherently evil by intellect.
B) Because the Law has made it prohibited due to the lack of capacity (al-mahalliyya) — a free person is not considered property, so the sale is annexed to what is evil by disposition.
C) Because it is evil due to an accompanying circumstance like the Friday adhan.
D) Because the Prophet (ﷺ) explicitly forbade it in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Acts evil for themselves are either inherently evil by intellect or annexed by law due to lack of capacity, and their prohibition renders them void from the start.
